    47→### BUG: Unhandled `result.status` for Successful Push  
    48→**Severity**: low  
    49→**Location**: POST  
    50→**Problem**: When `pushToGitHub(body)` is successful, `result.error` will be falsy, and the code proceeds to `return NextResponse.json(result.data)`. The current implementation always defaults to a 200 OK status because `NextResponse.json()` without a second argument defaults to `status: 200`. If `pushToGitHub` intends to convey a different success status, it's lost.

    29→  
    30→```typescript  
    31→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
    32→import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
    33→import { scanRepo } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    34→  
    35→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    36→  try {  
    37→    const body = await request.json()  
    38→  
    39→    if (!body.url || typeof body.url !== 'string') {  
    40→      return NextResponse.json(  
    41→        { error: 'Repository URL is required' },  
    42→        { status: 400 }  
    43→      )  
    44→    }  
    45→  
    46→    let ref = 'main';  
    47→    if (body.ref !== undefined && typeof body.ref !== 'string') {  
    48→      return NextResponse.json(  
    49→        { error: 'Repository reference (ref) must be a string if provided' },  
    50→        { status: 400 }  
    51→      );  
    52→    } else if (typeof body.ref === 'string') {  
    53→      ref = body.ref;  
    54→    }  
    55→  
    56→    const result = await scanRepo(body.url, ref)  
    57→  
    58→    if (result.error) {  
    59→      return NextResponse.json(  
    60→        { error: result.error },  
    61→        { status: result.status }  
    62→      )  
    63→    }  
    64→    return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    65→  } catch (error) {  
    66→    console.error('Error scanning repo:', error)  
    67→    // SyntaxError is thrown by request.json() when the body is not valid JSON  
    68→    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {  
    69→      return NextResponse.json(  
    70→        { error: 'Invalid request body' },  
    71→        { status: 400 }  
    72→      )  
    73→    }  
    74→    // All other errors (e.g. scanRepo throwing due to network/service failures) are internal  
    75→    return NextResponse.json(  
    76→      { error: 'Failed to scan repository due to an internal server error.' },  
    77→      { status: 500 }  
    78→    )  
    79→  }  
    80→}

    54→### BUG: Potential UI desync if `result.outputPath` is null/undefined  
    55→**Severity**: low  
    56→**Location**: `BuildAction` (JSX rendering)  
    57→**Problem**: In the JSX rendering section for the "Install command", there's a condition `isComplete && result.outputPath`. However, TypeScript's type narrowing might not fully carry through the JSX. If `result` is `null` or `undefined` at the point of `result.outputPath`, it would cause a runtime error. While `isComplete` implies `result` is not null, `result.outputPath` itself could still be `undefined` or `null` even if `isComplete` is true, depending on the `PluginBuildResult` type definition and the actual data received. The current code `result.outputPath` without optional chaining or a null check could lead to a runtime error if `outputPath` is not guaranteed to exist when `isComplete` is true.  
    58→**Fix**: Add optional chaining to `result.outputPath` in the JSX rendering for the install command to safely access the property.

20:### BUG: Incorrect `getSkillKey` for 'repo' type  
21:**Severity**: high  
23:**Problem**: The `getSkillKey` function for `repo` type skills uses `skill.url` and `skill.skillPath`. However, the `PluginSkillSelection` type for `repo` skills (as implied by `RepoScanner` and its `onAddSkill` prop) should include `repoId` and `skillId` to uniquely identify a skill within a scanned repository. Using `url` and `skillPath` might not be unique enough if multiple skills from the same path but different repos (or different versions of the same repo) are considered, or if the `skillPath` itself isn't unique across different skills within the same repo. More critically, the `RepoScanner` component's `onAddSkill` prop expects a `PluginSkillSelection` which, for `repo` type, should contain `repoId` and `skillId`. The current implementation of `getSkillKey` does not align with the expected structure of a `repo` skill as it would be added by `RepoScanner`.  
24:**Fix**: Update the `getSkillSelection` function to use `repoId` and `skillId` for `repo` type skills, assuming these properties are available on the `PluginSkillSelection` for `repo` type. This will ensure consistency and correct key generation for repository-based skills.

If `gw_list` contains characters that are special to `sed` (like `&`, `/`, `\`, `[`, `*`, etc.), `sed` will interpret them as part of the regular expression or replacement string, leading to incorrect substitutions or `sed` errors. 24:**Fix**: The `gw_list` variable needs to be escaped before being passed to `portable_sed` to ensure that any special characters it might contain are treated as literal strings. This can be done by using a similar escaping mechanism as `safe_dir`.

```
  // Clean up polling on unmount

      if (pollRef.current) clearInterval(pollRef.current)
```

```
  // Clean up polling on unmount — clearPoll is memoized so it is stable,
```

**Old:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  try {
    const body = await request.json()
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {
  // Parse the request body separately so a JSON parse failure is always a
  // client error (400), while errors from the service layer return 500.
  let body: unknown
  try {
    body = await request.json()
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Invalid request body' },
      { status: 400 }
    )
  }

  try {
    const result = await buildPlugin(body)

    if (result.error) {
      return NextResponse.json(
        { error: result.error },
        { status: result.status }
      )
    }
    return NextResponse.json(result.data, { status: result.status })
  } catch {
    return NextResponse.json(
      { error: 'Internal Server Error' },
      { status: 500 }
    )
  }
}
```

**Result:**

The file /Users/emanuelesabetta/ai-maestro/.claude/worktrees/rck-a84928/app/api/plugin-builder/build/route.ts has been updated successfully.

```
    if command -v claude &>/dev/null; then
        local claude_ver
        claude_ver=$(claude --version 2>/dev/null | head -n1 || echo "installed")
        maestro_check "Claude Code" "${claude_ver} ${GREEN}✓${NC}"
        HAS_CLAUDE=true
    else
        maestro_check "Claude Code" "${YELLOW}not found${NC}"
    fi

    # Codex
    if command -v codex &>/dev/null; then
        maestro_check "OpenAI Codex" "${GREEN}✓${NC}"
    else
        maestro_check "OpenAI Codex" "${DIM}not found${NC}"
    fi

    # Tailscale
    NEED_TAILSCALE=false
    if command -v tailscale &>/dev/null; then
        maestro_check "Tailscale" "${GREEN}✓${NC}"
    else
        maestro_check "Tailscale" "${DIM}not found${NC}"
        NEED_TAILSCALE=true
    fi
```

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:02:55]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I can see the exact issue. The `disabledReason` uses `!name.trim()` as the first branch, which only catches the empty case. But a name like `_foo` or `-foo` has a non-empty trim but still fails the regex — so the first branch misses it, the second branch catches it, but gives the wrong message ("letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores only" without mentioning the start-with-alphanumeric requirement). The fix per the findings is:  

1. `!name.trim()` stays as the empty check — shows "Enter a plugin name".  
2. The regex failure message must be updated to "Invalid plugin name (must start with a letter or number, only letters, numbers, hyphens, underscores allowed)".  

The logic structure is already correct (empty check first, then regex check), only the error message text needs updating to properly describe the constraint.

     2→ * Plugin Builder - Push to GitHub API

     4→ * POST /api/plugin-builder/push - Push manifest to user's fork

     7→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     8→import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
     9→import { pushToGitHub } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→import type { PluginPushConfig } from '@/types/plugin-builder'  
    11→  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {  
    14→    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig  
    15→  
    16→    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json(  
    18→        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },  
    19→        { status: 400 }  
    20→      )  
    21→    }  
    22→  
    23→    if (!body.manifest || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json(  
    25→        { error: 'Manifest is required' },  
    26→        { status: 400 }  
    27→      )  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)  
    31→  
    32→    if (result.error) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json(  
    34→        { error: result.error },  
    35→        { status: result.status }  
    36→      )  
    37→    }  
    38→    return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    39→  } catch (error) {  
    40→    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)  
    41→    return NextResponse.json(  
    42→      { error: 'Invalid request body' },  
    43→      { status: 400 }  
    44→    )  
    45→  }  
    46→}

## <span style="color:#FF9800">◈ SUB-AGENT</span>  *[2026-03-22 20:02:50]*

<div style="border-left: 4px solid #FF9800; padding-left: 12px; margin: 4px 0;">

I have read both files. Now I'll apply both fixes.  

**Fix 1:** The `body.manifest` check: `!body.manifest` is already truthy for `null` (since `!null === true`), but the condition `typeof body.manifest !== 'object'` combined with the `!body.manifest` creates a subtle logical gap. More importantly, the explicit `null` check makes the intent clear and correct: `typeof null === 'object'` so without the explicit null check, a `null` value that somehow passes `!body.manifest` (it won't since `!null` is `true`, but the intent should be explicit). The real fix needed is that `!body.manifest` does catch `null`, but the check order matters — let me verify: `!null` is `true`, so `null` IS caught by `!body.manifest`. However, the findings require adding the explicit `|| body.manifest === null` check for clarity and correctness, and also improving the error message to say "non-null object".  

**Fix 2:** Differentiate SyntaxError (400) from other errors (500) in the catch block.

     1→/**  
     2→ * Plugin Builder - Push to GitHub API  
     3→ *  
     4→ * POST /api/plugin-builder/push - Push manifest to user's fork  
     5→ */  
     6→  
     7→import { NextResponse } from 'next/server'  
     8→import type { NextRequest } from 'next/server'  
     9→import { pushToGitHub } from '@/services/plugin-builder-service'  
    10→import type { PluginPushConfig } from '@/types/plugin-builder'  
    11→  
    12→export async function POST(request: NextRequest) {  
    13→  try {  
    14→    const body = await request.json() as PluginPushConfig  
    15→  
    16→    if (!body.forkUrl || typeof body.forkUrl !== 'string') {  
    17→      return NextResponse.json(  
    18→        { error: 'Fork URL is required' },  
    19→        { status: 400 }  
    20→      )  
    21→    }  
    22→  
    23→    if (!body.manifest || body.manifest === null || typeof body.manifest !== 'object') {  
    24→      return NextResponse.json(  
    25→        { error: 'Manifest is required and must be a non-null object' },  
    26→        { status: 400 }  
    27→      )  
    28→    }  
    29→  
    30→    const result = await pushToGitHub(body)  
    31→  
    32→    if (result.error) {  
    33→      return NextResponse.json(  
    34→        { error: result.error },  
    35→        { status: result.status }  
    36→      )  
    37→    }  
    38→    return NextResponse.json(result.data)  
    39→  } catch (error) {  
    40→    console.error('Error pushing to GitHub:', error)  
    41→    // SyntaxError is thrown by request.json() when the body is not valid JSON  
    42→    if (error instanceof SyntaxError) {  
    43→      return NextResponse.json(  
    44→        { error: 'Invalid JSON in request body' },  
    45→        { status: 400 }  
    46→      )  
    47→    }  
    48→    return NextResponse.json(  
    49→      { error: 'Internal server error' },  
    50→      { status: 500 }  
    51→    )  
    52→  }  
    53→}

- `PURPLE`, `CYAN`, `BOLD` are defined at lines 25-27 as part of the color palette, and cleared in 2 places (line 40 and line 1343). They are genuinely never used in any string interpolation. But removing them from the top palette would be the proper root fix. I'll remove all assignments of `PURPLE`, `CYAN`, `BOLD` from the color sections.  

- `NEED_CLAUDE` (line 798), `HAS_CODEX` (line 804), `HAS_TAILSCALE` (line 826): These are SET in two places — once during the preflight check function (lines 546-575) and again in the installation block. The values set in the installation block (lines 798, 804, 826) are never subsequently read — they are write-only in that second location. The proper fix is to remove those redundant assignments from lines 798, 804, and 826.  

- SC2016 (line 1061): single-quoted sed pattern `'s|...|...:${PORT}|'` — `${PORT}` won't expand. Change to double quotes: `"s|...|...:${PORT}|"`.  

- SC2086 (lines 1105, 1126, 1161, 1198, 1233): `${PORT}` in curl URLs needs quoting as `"${PORT}"`.

   307→export async function buildPlugin(config: PluginBuildConfig): Promise<ServiceResult<PluginBuildResult>> {  
   308→  // Validate inputs (protects both Next.js routes and headless router)  
   309→  const validationError = validateBuildConfig(config)  
   310→  if (validationError) {  
   311→    return { error: validationError, status: 400 }  
   312→  }  
   313→  
   314→  // Concurrency guard  
   315→  if (activeOps >= MAX_CONCURRENT_OPS) {  
   316→    return { error: 'Too many concurrent builds. Please wait and try again.', status: 429 }  
   317→  }  
   318→  
   319→  try {  
   320→    // Evict stale builds before adding new ones  
   321→    evictStaleBuildResults()  
   322→  
   323→    activeOps++  
   324→    const buildId = randomUUID()  
   325→    const buildDir = path.join(BUILDS_DIR, buildId)  
   326→  
   327→    // Create build directory  
   328→    await fs.mkdir(buildDir, { recursive: true })  
   329→  
   330→    // Generate manifest  
   331→    const manifest = generateManifest(config)  
   332→  
   333→    // Write manifest to build directory  
   334→    await fs.writeFile(  
   335→      path.join(buildDir, 'plugin.manifest.json'),  
   336→      JSON.stringify(manifest, null, 2)  
   337→    )  
   338→

   182→    }

```
    // Run build asynchronously
    runBuild(buildId, buildDir, manifest).catch(err => {
      console.error(`Build ${buildId} failed:`, err)
      // Ensure status is updated even on unexpected errors
      const r = buildResults.get(buildId)
      if (r && r.status === 'building') {
        buildResults.set(buildId, {
          ...r,
          status: 'failed',
          logs: [err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err)],
        })
      }
    }).finally(() => {
      activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)
    })

    return { data: result, status: 202 }
  } catch (error) {
    activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)
    console.error('Error starting plugin build:', error)
    return { error: 'Failed to start plugin build', status: 500 }
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
    // Run build asynchronously; activeOps is decremented in the outer finally block
    // once the build is fully launched (or the launch itself fails).
    runBuild(buildId, buildDir, manifest).catch(err => {
      console.error(`Build ${buildId} failed:`, err)
      // Ensure status is updated even on unexpected errors
      const r = buildResults.get(buildId)
      if (r && r.status === 'building') {
        buildResults.set(buildId, {
          ...r,
          status: 'failed',
          logs: [err instanceof Error ? err.message : String(err)],
        })
      }
    })

    return { data: result, status: 202 }
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Error starting plugin build:', error)
    return { error: 'Failed to start plugin build', status: 500 }
  } finally {
    // Decrement exactly once, whether the try succeeded or threw.
    activeOps = Math.max(0, activeOps - 1)
  }
}
```


**New:**  
```
function sanitizeSourceName(url: string): string {
  const sanitized = url
    .replace(/^https?:\/\//, '')
    .replace(/\.git$/, '')
    .replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9-]/g, '-')
    .replace(/-+/g, '-')
    .replace(/^-|-$/g, '')
    .slice(0, 40)
  // Guard against URLs whose entire content was stripped (e.g. "https://-.git")
  return sanitized || 'unknown-source'
}
```

**New:**

```
// Run eviction every 10 minutes.
// Wrap in try-catch so an unexpected throw does not silently kill the interval.
const evictionInterval = setInterval(() => {
  try {
    evictStaleBuildResults()
  } catch (err) {
    console.error('Error during build result eviction:', err)
  }
}, 10 * 60 * 1000)
evictionInterval.unref() // Don't prevent process exit
```

**Old:**  
```
                maestro_step 1 4 "Pulling latest changes..." ""
                cd "$INSTALL_DIR"
                # Count stashes before so we only pop what we pushed (avoids race condition)
                local stash_count_before
                stash_count_before=$(git stash list 2>/dev/null | wc -l | tr -d ' ')
                git stash --quiet 2>/dev/null || true
                local stash_count_after
                stash_count_after=$(git stash list 2>/dev/null | wc -l | tr -d ' ')
                local had_stash=false
                if [ "$stash_count_after" -gt "$stash_count_before" ]; then
                    had_stash=true
                fi
```

**New:**  
```
                maestro_step 1 4 "Pulling latest changes..." ""
                cd "$INSTALL_DIR"
                # Use git stash exit status to detect whether a stash was created:
                # exit 0 = stash created, exit 1 = nothing to stash (no local changes).
                # This avoids the race condition of comparing stash counts before/after.
                local had_stash=false
                if git stash --quiet 2>/dev/null; then had_stash=true; else had_stash=false; fi
```

**Fix 2: `act5_grand_finale` — only call `tmux new-session` when the session does NOT exist, then always call `tmux attach-session`.**  

Looking at the current code (lines 1284-1295), the structure is:  
```
if tmux has-session ... (exists):
    print info message
else:
    tmux new-session ...
fi
sleep 2
tmux attach-session ...
```

Wait, let me re-read the exact current code to verify before editing.  

The current code at lines 1283-1295:  
```
            if tmux has-session -t "my-first-agent" 2>/dev/null; then
                maestro_info "Reattaching to existing 'my-first-agent' session..."
            else
                tmux new-session -d -s "my-first-agent" -c "$AGENT_DIR" \
                    "$AI_TOOL \"$INITIAL_PROMPT\""
            fi
            sleep 2
            tmux attach-session -t "my-first-agent"
```

The bug report says "the script calls `tmux new-session` even if a session already exists." But looking at the code, the `if/else` structure already prevents that — `new-session` is only called in the `else` branch. However, `sleep 2` is always executed regardless of whether a new session was created or not. The `sleep 2` before `attach-session` is only needed when a new session was just created (to give it time to start). The fix requested is to move `sleep 2` inside the `else` branch, and ensure `tmux attach-session` is always called.  

The prompt says: "only call `tmux new-session` if the session does NOT exist, then always call `tmux attach-session`." The current code already does this structurally but the `sleep 2` is outside the `else`. Let me apply the fix as specified to move `sleep 2` inside the new-session branch and keep `attach-session` always called:  

</div>

   269→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   270→// Utility helpers  
   271→// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------  
   272→  
   273→async function readJsonBody(req: IncomingMessage): Promise<any> {  
   274→  return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {  
   275→    const chunks: Buffer[] = []  
   276→    req.on('data', (chunk: Buffer) => chunks.push(chunk))  
   277→    req.on('end', () => {  
   278→      const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf-8')  
   279→      if (!body) return resolve({})  
   280→      try {  
   281→        resolve(JSON.parse(body))  
   282→      } catch (e) {  
   283→        reject(new Error('Invalid JSON body'))  
   284→      }  
   285→    })  
   286→    req.on('error', reject)  
   287→  })  
   288→}

**Old:**  
```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  if (result.error && !result.data) {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 500, { error: result.error }, result.headers)
  } else {
    sendJson(res, result.status || 200, result.data, result.headers)
  }
}
```

**New:**  
```
function sendServiceResult(res: ServerResponse, result: any) {
  // Always honour result.status when provided — a service may return 201, 204, etc.
  const statusCode = result.status || (result.error ? 500 : 200)
  const body = result.error ? { error: result.error } : result.data
  sendJson(res, statusCode, body, result.headers)
}
```

**Result:**
